  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_56a9790e-189c-4d60-86cb-99260b9a6ba1'

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer11436104329378099279"><i>Of Bees and Mist</i> is an engrossing fable that chronicles three generations of women under one family tree and places them in a mythical town where spirits and spells, witchcraft and demons, and prophets and clairvoyance are an everyday reality.<br/><br/>Meridia grows up in a lonely home until she falls in love with Daniel at age sixteen. Soon, they marry, and Meridia can finally esca</span>
  <span id="freeText11436104329378099279" style="display:none"><i>Of Bees and Mist</i> is an engrossing fable that chronicles three generations of women under one family tree and places them in a mythical town where spirits and spells, witchcraft and demons, and prophets and clairvoyance are an everyday reality.<br /><br />Meridia grows up in a lonely home until she falls in love with Daniel at age sixteen. Soon, they marry, and Meridia can finally escape to live with her charming husband’s family—unaware that they harbor dark mysteries of their own. As Meridia struggles to embrace her life as a young bride, she discovers long-kept secrets about her own past as well as shocking truths about her new family that push her love, courage, and sanity to the brink.<br /><br />Erick Setiawan’s astonishing debut is a richly atmospheric and tumultuous ride of hope and heartbreak that is altogether touching, truthful, and memorable.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11436104329378099279" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/71590229?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=table">table</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=sshh-family-secrets">sshh-family-secrets</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer71590229" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2055767826271292294">i wish i liked this more, i truly do. it's in the running for best cover of the year, which is of course why i bought it (in hardcover, before reading any reviews of it, and barely reading the flap-copy) but it seemed like my brand of tea - crumbling houses, family secrets, a touch of magic realism. only it was more than a touch. this is basically a fairy tale. which hit me unexpectedly as i was reading. but it's fine, i acclimate to the tone and continue reading... it's just that it's not very </span>
  <span id="freeText2055767826271292294" style="display:none">i wish i liked this more, i truly do. it's in the running for best cover of the year, which is of course why i bought it (in hardcover, before reading any reviews of it, and barely reading the flap-copy) but it seemed like my brand of tea - crumbling houses, family secrets, a touch of magic realism. only it was more than a touch. this is basically a fairy tale. which hit me unexpectedly as i was reading. but it's fine, i acclimate to the tone and continue reading... it's just that it's not very tidy. there is a fascinating story in here, it's just muddled underneath other half-stories. magical realism is tempting for a writer because problems and conflicts can be resolved in any way the author chooses, without worrying about expectations or truth-feeling. but it's easy to let the story slip away under such circumstances. and that may have happened here. i still cared about the characters, and appreciated that it stuck to common fairy-tale ground like wicked stepmothers (or in-laws) and true love marred by magic and fate etc, but usually in a fairy tale, at least SOMEONE is happy. i would definitely read a second book by this author. please.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2055767826271292294" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggie Stiefvater" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggie Stiefvater" href="/user/show/1246837-maggie-stiefvater">Maggie Stiefvater</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1246837-maggie-stiefvater?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1246837-maggie-stiefvater?shelf=recommended">recommended</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer82329408" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11997961407475308422">Almost exactly two hours ago, I finished reading OF BEES AND MIST, and I’m still in its spell. Normally I am opposed to writing reviews right after I read a book, because often my opinion of a book needs time to sort of marinate. I tend to get fonder of a book the longer I’ve had to think, but I have to say, my fondness for this book is pretty darn inconsequential. What matters is that this curious novel has dug its way under my skin in a way I can tell will last for quite awhile. Saying that OF</span>
  <span id="freeText11997961407475308422" style="display:none">Almost exactly two hours ago, I finished reading OF BEES AND MIST, and I’m still in its spell. Normally I am opposed to writing reviews right after I read a book, because often my opinion of a book needs time to sort of marinate. I tend to get fonder of a book the longer I’ve had to think, but I have to say, my fondness for this book is pretty darn inconsequential. What matters is that this curious novel has dug its way under my skin in a way I can tell will last for quite awhile. Saying that OF BEES AND MIST is a fable-like story of two women -- one whose birth home is infested by perpetual mist and one who literally whispers bees -- who are locked in furious and long-lasted battle is rather inadequate. If I add that its chapters are hung lusciously with metaphor (see what I did there?) I get a little closer. <br /><br />But the real charm and danger both of this book are the familial relationships. Because the two women at the heart of the book (though there are many -- for a book written by a man, I’m pretty much blown away by the scads of nuanced, strong women in this novel)(he has possibly stolen my estrogen)(it’s all right, he’s making good use of it), Eva and Meridia, are mother-in-law and daughter-in-law. Their common link is a pleasant but flawed man, and the way that the author paints the relationship between mother, daughter-in-law, husband, sister-in-law, etc. etc. is very familiar for all its magic realism trappings. <br /><br />Meridia escapes from a troubled home life directly into the arms of Daniel, a guileless young man. From him she inherits a complicated family drama ultimately controlled by Eva, who is a wicked stepmother in the most horrifying and delicious meaning of the phrase. Anyone who has had the slightest amount of conflict with their in-laws or extended family will appreciate the subtleties and motivations of every character in OF BEES. Events and what each party’s perception of events are often delightfully confused. This is young, married life, served with family-sized side dishes of guilt trips, subtext, and meaningful looks. Definitely enough to share and enough again to take home for later. But there’s joy, too, and charm aplenty, and some moments stark and moving in their suddenly unsentimental view of love. <br /><br />A clever tale like this, brimming with none-so-subtle metaphors and magic, could easily be an intriguing exercise in the fantastic and mundane, but the reason OF BEES is getting put here in my five-stars category is that the characters evoked genuine emotion and sympathy from me. The phrase “flawed, strong heroine” is thrown around too much, but Meridia is that if I’ve ever seen one. She makes bad choices, hard choices, but she always makes A choice and you’re always convinced she’s the hero regardless; her goodness is not in question. Normally, I can’t tolerate infidelity plotlines but infidelity in this case was necessary (though agonizing). This book was both a pleasure and a pain to read and I’m so glad I picked it up -- entirely by chance, while rushing through the store on the way out of town. Might’ve been the work of fate or of the engineering spirits, if OF BEES AND MIST is to be believed.<br /><br /><br />***wondering why all my reviews are five stars? Because I'm only reviewing my favorite books -- not every book I read. Consider a novel's presence on my Goodreads bookshelf as a hearty endorsement. I can't believe I just said "hearty." It sounds like a stew.***</span>
  <a data-text-id="11997961407475308422" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14205502657847091687"><b>Because Jess says:</b><br/><br/><i>PS: If you don't love this book then.... <br/><br/>Just please love this book! :) </i><br/><br/>Never fear my relationship with my #humanbestie remains intact… for the time being anyways. *side-eyes <u>The Stranger</u>* <br/><br/><b>5 words CAN break your heart Stars</b><br/><br/>I fell in love with <u>Of Bees and Mist</u> so slowly and entirely that it was not until I had put it down that I realized how completely it had consumed my thoughts.   <span id="freeText14205502657847091687" style="display:none"><b>Because Jess says:</b><br><br><i>PS: If you don't love this book then.... <br><br>Just please love this book! :) </i><br><br>Never fear my relationship with my #humanbestie remains intact… for the time being anyways. *side-eyes <u>The Stranger</u>* <br><br><b>5 words CAN break your heart Stars</b><br><br>I fell in love with <u>Of Bees and Mist</u> so slowly and entirely that it was not until I had put it down that I realized how completely it had consumed my thoughts. How deeply Setiawan’s words and characters had wound themselves around my bitter, black heart. But don’t take <b>my</b> word for it; here are some of his:<br><br><i>The small talk that sprang readily to their lips came to hers only with a tremendous effort. After an opportunity had come and gone, she often scolded herself for not saying this or doing that, for laughing too loud or smiling too little. Whenever she tried to re-create the moment of contact, she was easily rebuffed by the slightest gesture, withdrawing all too quickly if she thought she was in the way. The old stone-and-brick schoolhouse, with its four gabled roofs and round little windows, was the only thing that seemed steadfast to her, while the beings that populated its rooms and thundered down its corridors were unreal and unpredictable. It gripped her like a monstrous truth that she was condemned to lead life without belonging or feeling close to anyone.</i><br><br>While there is magic present in this world it never carries the actual story here but rather <b>compliments</b> a story of love’s disillusions. It is more like magical symbolism than anything, the bees and mists of the title came to represent the bitter sting of cruel words and the manifestations of the impenetrable walls that lies and infidelity create. <br><br>At its core this isn’t a supernatural story, it is a story of humanity's imperfections and how you cope with a life that is less perfect than the one you had planned for yourself. When life heaps on the monotony and flaws of everyday life how does the dream of love survive? How many cruel selfish actions does it take to finally destroy it? <br><br>Meridia was eighteen when she met Daniel, a handsome carefree young man. They fell desperately in love, the kind of consumptive love that only the foolish or very young can seem to experience. As is generally the case, life doesn’t let Meridia’s naiveté go unpunished. Nor Daniel’s. There is a lot going on in this novel; first love, heartbreak, deception, cruelty and stubbornness, to name but a few. <br><br>My heart soared and broke apart with these characters stories. So many moments and passages left me breathless with wonder and heartbreak for them. <br><br><i>Don't you see? They are both extreme and exacting creatures. When they love, it is so complete they can tolerate no defects. Ask them to die for each other and they will drag a sword across their throat without hesitation. But ask them to blunt their edges, to endure arguments and daily imperfections, and they will despise each other to no end.</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487711369i/22043813._SX540_.jpg" width="434" height="287.7" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_248461221" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/248461221" />
    <a title="Jess ❈Harbinger of Blood-Soaked Rainbows❈" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7125124-jess-harbinger-of-blood-soaked-rainbows"><img alt="Jess ❈Harbinger of Blood-Soaked Rainbows❈" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1440512431p2/7125124.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/248461221?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jess ❈Harbinger of Blood-Soaked Rainbows❈" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jess ❈Harbinger of Blood-Soaked Rainbows❈" href="/user/show/7125124-jess-harbinger-of-blood-soaked-rainbows">Jess ❈Harbinger of Blood-Soaked Rainbows❈</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7125124-jess-harbinger-of-blood-soaked-rainbows?shelf=top-10">top-10</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7125124-jess-harbinger-of-blood-soaked-rainbows?shelf=best-ever-favorites">best-ever-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7125124-jess-harbinger-of-blood-soaked-rainbows?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7125124-jess-harbinger-of-blood-soaked-rainbows?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7125124-jess-harbinger-of-blood-soaked-rainbows?shelf=a-bit-o-magical-realism">a-bit-o-magical-realism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7125124-jess-harbinger-of-blood-soaked-rainbows?shelf=someone-needs-a-punch-in-the-face">someone-needs-a-punch-in-the-face</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7125124-jess-harbinger-of-blood-soaked-rainbows?shelf=bizarrelandia">bizarrelandia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7125124-jess-harbinger-of-blood-soaked-rainbows?shelf=top-100">top-100</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer248461221" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2665856970217407582">In light of my human bestie just having read this and loved it, and also in celebration of this same human bestie's forthcoming trip to ME (8 days!), I am bumping this review because I loved this book so hard and am feeling the need to 're-read it soon.<br/><br/>________<br/>This is a very hard book to review, since I don't think I've ever read anything else like it, and I'm not likely to in my lifetime. I don't really know how to describe this book. Others have called it magical realism, a fairy-tale, a fable</span>
  <span id="freeText2665856970217407582" style="display:none">In light of my human bestie just having read this and loved it, and also in celebration of this same human bestie's forthcoming trip to ME (8 days!), I am bumping this review because I loved this book so hard and am feeling the need to 're-read it soon.<br /><br />________<br />This is a very hard book to review, since I don't think I've ever read anything else like it, and I'm not likely to in my lifetime. I don't really know how to describe this book. Others have called it magical realism, a fairy-tale, a fable.....and I'm not sure which category this novel seems to fit into. None very cleanly, that is.<br /><br />Meridia is kind of a lost soul. She is sad and lonely, with very few friends, a cold mother and distant father, and is stuck in an old house with nobody to talk to and nobody to look up to. She meets Daniel when she is sixteen and is immediately swept into a beautiful fairy-tale love story when they marry and Meridia leaves her home to live with Daniel's family. Who at first seem pretty great, but once the illusions become unnecessary, Meridia finds herself in even more of a nightmare than the one she left.<br /><br />Clairvoyance and magic are an everyday reality in the fictional town which serves as the setting. I know that some people who read this took an issue with this, but it didn't bother me at all. In fact, I found it refreshing to read a book where all the rules have been thrown out. Eric Setiawan also writes beautifully, and his poetic tone really added to the overall eerie atmosphere of the book. The characters are also extremely interesting and multi-faceted, and I loved learning new things about them and seeing their layers unravel as the plot thickens. This is a fairy-tale of sorts, one that is even more twisted than one the Brothers Grimm thought up. Daniel and Meridia have a beautiful love story that is strained, pulled, and twisted by familial and social circumstances. In a way, this fairy-tale serves also as an allegory and a fable as well, as every mystical creation has a deeper meaning. <br /><br />All magic aside, the core of this novel is the survival of love amidst hard and cruel circumstances; whether they be family loyalties, or the threat of poverty, or even the dissipation of the fairy-tale romance that every relationship is fated to encounter. At times, this novel is heartbreaking, at times very moving. I was very sorry for it to end, and wish that actually this novel had been double its length. Like Neil Gaiman's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15783514.The_Ocean_at_the_End_of_the_Lane" title="The Ocean at the End of the Lane by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">The Ocean at the End of the Lane</a>, <i>Of Bees and Mist</i> made me long to stay in this mystical world a bit longer because I knew that there were secrets left to uncover, people left to meet, and more to this story than the one which ended on the last page. 5 beautiful, wonderful, mystical stars. I can't wait to re-read this soon.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2665856970217407582" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_926858173" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/926858173" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25478105-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1462374579p2/25478105.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/926858173?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/25478105-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789022959695" href="/book/show/8331309-over-bijen-en-mist">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25478105-anne?shelf=purdycovers">purdycovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25478105-anne?shelf=shit">shit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25478105-anne?shelf=waste-of-time">waste-of-time</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer926858173" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1257952265141141745">It started out as something I thought I would enjoy: a fairy tale for adults. As the story progressed, I started to like it less and less. I don't know if it was partly due to the Dutch translation, but it all felt like the use of language was very cliché and something I could've written myself. <br/>Somewhere halfway through the book, all (to me) irritating things were starting to add up and I was very close to giving up on it entirely. What irritating things you wonder?<br/><br/>1. <b>How many times do you have</b></span>
  <span id="freeText1257952265141141745" style="display:none">It started out as something I thought I would enjoy: a fairy tale for adults. As the story progressed, I started to like it less and less. I don't know if it was partly due to the Dutch translation, but it all felt like the use of language was very cliché and something I could've written myself. <br />Somewhere halfway through the book, all (to me) irritating things were starting to add up and I was very close to giving up on it entirely. What irritating things you wonder?<br /><br />1. <b>How many times do you have to use the word 'womb'?</b> I actually thought of counting the number of times myself, but then thought it was a waste of my time. When I get really bored at some point, I might still do it and add it here, just to give an indication on how ridiculously often this word is being used.<br />2. The stepmother is evil. Still evil. You thought she wasn't evil? She's evil. Yup, very evil. And still is. <b>OKAY, WE GET IT, SHE'S EVIL!!!</b> I actually said this (after a wee bit of cursing) out loud after reading this sentence: "The next morning, Patina showed up on Willow Lane with welts on her face and cigarette burns on her hands." Seriously?<br />3. How come every character in this book annoys the living feces out of me? They're all caricatures of themselves. I hated pretty much all of the adult male characters, especially Daniel. The only character I somewhat liked was Meridia, the main character, which was vital to making me able to finish this book. Still, her naivety was something I could barely stand as well. The same goes for the lack of willpower in the beginning of the story. Why would you stay in such a terrible house and with such a [insert bad word] of a husband. <br />4.Then there were the vulgar scenes and language which I didn't understand the usage of except maybe the author trying to make it clear that this is an ADULT fairy tale. I don't think that this is the way to do it. Adding a couple of obscene scenes to a Harry Potter book doesn't put an adult-stamp on it either; it just makes it look ridiculous and inappropriate.<br /><br />One thing I'm wondering about is Ahab's home country: "Try us, and we'll ship you back ass first to the windmill hell you came from!". Was this a reference to Holland? <br /><br />Anyhow, why not give this book one star instead of two after all this negative ranting? Because I finished it in about a week and was hoping for something unexpectedly interesting to happen. So it kept me going until the end. Don't get me started on the ending by the way...Something about forgiving and letting go. No way.<br /><br />EDIT: I'm giving this book 1 star anyways because every time I think of it, I get annoyed all over again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1257952265141141745" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_137574561" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/137574561?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Yolanda Sfetsos" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Yolanda Sfetsos" href="/user/show/4724592-yolanda-sfetsos">Yolanda Sfetsos</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780755348541" href="/book/show/6438481-of-bees-and-mist">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4724592-yolanda-sfetsos?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer137574561" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer118167987421403605">This is Erick Setiawan's first novel. I was so impressed that I can't wait to see what else he's got to offer in the future.<br/><br/>At the core of the story is the life of Meridia and the people who come in and out of her life as she grows from an insecure child, into a very clever and strong woman. It all starts with her very strange parents and the cold house with ghosts in the mirrors and shadows on the walls. Then follows her life with the family she becomes a part of after she marries the love of h</span>
  <span id="freeText118167987421403605" style="display:none">This is Erick Setiawan's first novel. I was so impressed that I can't wait to see what else he's got to offer in the future.<br /><br />At the core of the story is the life of Meridia and the people who come in and out of her life as she grows from an insecure child, into a very clever and strong woman. It all starts with her very strange parents and the cold house with ghosts in the mirrors and shadows on the walls. Then follows her life with the family she becomes a part of after she marries the love of her life, Daniel. Growing up in a home where her mother often forgot her, and her father disappeared in a cloud of mist every night, living with Daniel's family should be a change for the better, right? <br /><br />Unfortunately, with a mother-in-law that uses bees to enrage the members of her family - as well as plays them agaisnt one another - Meridia soon discovers that her new home is as full of secrets as the one she grew up in.<br /><br />I loved this book so much that I couldn't wait to get back to it every time I had to put it down, and had to read it in long stretches. I just couldn't put it down! It was well written, unique, lyrical, and so filled with emotion that I found some scenes overwhelming. The antagonist does such horrible things and puts her family through so much that I kept hoping she would fade away, like other characters did.<br /><br />This is an outstanding book, a total keeper that is very hard to categorise because of it's unique, atmospheric, and very touching story about the trials of family, spun in a remarkable web of fantasy.<br /><br /><i>Of Bees and Mist</i> is a captivating book that'll sweep you up into a cloud of mystical wonder and keep you glued from start to finish by the vivid imagery, interesting characters, the magic of every word, and the constant heartbreak of the central character.</span>

          </span>

    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8200640-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/294482550?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/8200640-sarah">Sarah</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer294482550" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16739252649087544155">This is quite possibly my favorite book ever.<br/><br/>I lament the lack of grown-up fantasy novels, but this book delivers on that an so much more. It's more than just, "Look at this cool world I've thought up" and angst-y love triangles tropes that I see in too many of the stories I read. This book has depth, and the fantastic elements are just metaphors made tangible, a world steeped in magic but still filled with real. human emotions.<br/><br/>The whole book is permeated by the melancholy of lost love. The agai</span>
  <span id="freeText16739252649087544155" style="display:none">This is quite possibly my favorite book ever.<br /><br />I lament the lack of grown-up fantasy novels, but this book delivers on that an so much more. It's more than just, "Look at this cool world I've thought up" and angst-y love triangles tropes that I see in too many of the stories I read. This book has depth, and the fantastic elements are just metaphors made tangible, a world steeped in magic but still filled with real. human emotions.<br /><br />The whole book is permeated by the melancholy of lost love. The against-all-odds lovers are there, in the form of a girl who is often quite literally invisible and the boy who finally sees her. His mother makes for a delightfully twisted villain, one with a droning army of bees at her disposal. It's a roller coaster as Meridia and her husband struggle to escape his mother's clutches and to keep their marriage alive. Meridia's parents' marriage, failed though not ended, seems to foreshadow an unhappy ending. <br /><br />Although her husband can be weak and spineless, I found myself rooting for their reconciliation. <br /><br />And we all know I'm a sucker for a happy ending.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16739252649087544155" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1311306493" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1311306493" />
    <a title="Taryn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13977687-taryn"><img alt="Taryn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591322913p2/13977687.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1311306493?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Taryn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Taryn" href="/user/show/13977687-taryn">Taryn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13977687-taryn?shelf=bipoc-author">bipoc-author</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1311306493" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10339722369025019850">Oh my heart!<br/><br/>I am so, so, SO glad I read this while on Thanksgiving break from work. If I’d tried to read it during the usual midweek hustle-bustle of life, there’s no way I could have slowed down enough to hang with it. And it would have been my loss, because holy peppercorns can Erick Setiawan write.<br/><br/>And that’s pretty cool in itself, because if you read his <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2839569.Erick_Setiawan' rel='nofollow noopener'>(very funny) bio</a>, he’s not a native English speaker and has harbored doubts about his writing ability, going so far as to get an advanced de</span>
  <span id="freeText10339722369025019850" style="display:none">Oh my heart!<br /><br />I am so, so, SO glad I read this while on Thanksgiving break from work. If I’d tried to read it during the usual midweek hustle-bustle of life, there’s no way I could have slowed down enough to hang with it. And it would have been my loss, because holy peppercorns can Erick Setiawan write.<br /><br />And that’s pretty cool in itself, because if you read his <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2839569.Erick_Setiawan" rel="nofollow noopener">(very funny) bio</a>, he’s not a native English speaker and has harbored doubts about his writing ability, going so far as to get an advanced degree in computer science because it felt more accessible. <br /><br />That he pursued his dream of fiction writing instead of churning out software code is our good fortune. Of Bees and Mist is basically a 400-page fairy tale for adults. If you’re looking to recreate the feeling of sitting on your grandmother’s lap as she told one more story before bedtime, this book will do it. <br /><br />Meridia suffers a cold and isolated childhood with a distant, raging mother and critical, imperious father. Mists of varying colors surround their house by day and night, mysteriously ushering in and out strong emotions and heart-stopping betrayals. When Meridia meets an enchanting stranger at a fair in town, escape from her sadness finally seems possible. Unfortunately, married life brings unending trouble of its own, this time in the guise of her tempestuous mother-in-law, who exhales swarms of bees as she airs her grievances. <br /><br />It’s one of the best feats of sustained magical realism I’ve ever read. And despite its surreal quality, I was hopelessly invested in the characters. I read the last pages with my heart in my mouth. <br /><br />This isn’t the kind of book you can successfully read in ten-minute chunks. It needs time and space to breathe, to take root in your mind. For best results, wait for life to settle and slow, and serve with a hot beverage and a blanket.<br /><br />More book recommendations by me at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.readingwithhippos.com">www.readingwithhippos.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10339722369025019850" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1311306493">
  <td colspan="2">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1713491310" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7131816380260573199">I don't think it is going to be easy to review this without giving too much away, because most of what I didn't like about it is to do with the direction of the plot in the second half. I was really enjoying the whimsical nature and magical realism of the first half, but in the second it turns into this petty, repetitive family drama, pretty much all "he said, she said". I couldn't stand the negativity of all the characters, even those we're clearly meant to be rooting for. I'm quite honestly ba</span>
  <span id="freeText7131816380260573199" style="display:none">I don't think it is going to be easy to review this without giving too much away, because most of what I didn't like about it is to do with the direction of the plot in the second half. I was really enjoying the whimsical nature and magical realism of the first half, but in the second it turns into this petty, repetitive family drama, pretty much all "he said, she said". I couldn't stand the negativity of all the characters, even those we're clearly meant to be rooting for. I'm quite honestly baffled by a lot characterisation and the decisions made by the characters. And actually some of the author's treatment of certain characters made be feel downright uncomfortable. For example, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[vilifying Ahab the "foreigner" as some kind of monster, and the terrible one-sided depiction of Eva the monster-in-law <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I'm really disappointed that this book turned out to be so hateful, as it seemed to have all the elements I was looking for, in particular, escapist, lyrical magical realism and a focus on strong female characters. Unfortunately, this is not a book I can recommend.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7131816380260573199" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Jo Barton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2090731-jo-barton"><img alt="Jo Barton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1366880767p2/2090731.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/74700823?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo Barton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo Barton" href="/user/show/2090731-jo-barton">Jo Barton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780755348534" href="/book/show/6438480-of-bees-and-mist">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jo Barton by: </span>
      newbooksmagazine
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer74700823" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13977995554094645532">Set against a backdrop of a fantasy world we are introduced to two warring families who live their lives amidst magic and chicanery. Loaded with superstition and alive with intrigue, this is a stunning debut novel. In many ways this magical fantasy has several parallels with our modern world, yet we are never informed of time or place. It could be happening in the past or way ahead into our future. It is quite simply a novel of good versus evil, with the depth of characterisation lending an adde</span>
  <span id="freeText13977995554094645532" style="display:none">Set against a backdrop of a fantasy world we are introduced to two warring families who live their lives amidst magic and chicanery. Loaded with superstition and alive with intrigue, this is a stunning debut novel. In many ways this magical fantasy has several parallels with our modern world, yet we are never informed of time or place. It could be happening in the past or way ahead into our future. It is quite simply a novel of good versus evil, with the depth of characterisation lending an added dimension to the narrative. The outstanding quality of the writing makes the story come alive on so many levels: initially we feel the distress, witness the horrors and seethe against the injustice and then find it in ourselves to forgive the transgressions and laugh out loud at the witticisms.<br />This is an adult fairy tale with a difference. The underlying theme of love, loss and betrayal is expertly captured in a story that will live on in the imagination. I really enjoyed it.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13977995554094645532" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/716960524" />
    <a title="Jules" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4824134-jules"><img alt="Jules" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1561752629p2/4824134.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/716960524?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jules" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jules" href="/user/show/4824134-jules">Jules</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4824134-jules?shelf=weird-and-wonderful">weird-and-wonderful</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer716960524" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3460526971849109633"><br/>Wow, what a magical fable! <br/><br/>I was worried this book would focus too much on fantasy rather than feeling, and prove to be a bit shallow. What I didn't realise, was that I was going to get dragged into a both wonderful and harrowing world where feelings were expressed through that magic and fantasy. <br/><br/>It's as if all the feelings I experienced while reading this book came to life, be it in the form of mist, scents, ailments, the buzzing of bees, or the twinkle of fireflies. <br/><br/>I have honestly never read </span>
  <span id="freeText3460526971849109633" style="display:none"><br />Wow, what a magical fable! <br /><br />I was worried this book would focus too much on fantasy rather than feeling, and prove to be a bit shallow. What I didn't realise, was that I was going to get dragged into a both wonderful and harrowing world where feelings were expressed through that magic and fantasy. <br /><br />It's as if all the feelings I experienced while reading this book came to life, be it in the form of mist, scents, ailments, the buzzing of bees, or the twinkle of fireflies. <br /><br />I have honestly never read anything quite like this. It's a fairytale for adults. You'll experience hurt, fear, love, marriage, birth, death, trust, deceit and hope as you travel through this magical journey of life, love and loss. <br /><br />This tale has found a home in my heart, and I will never look at a bee, or the sea fog that approaches my house in the same way again!</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/55987543?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/372701-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Sarah by: </span>
      Anna
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/372701-sarah?shelf=fancypants">fancypants</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/372701-sarah?shelf=swords-and-sorcerors">swords-and-sorcerors</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer55987543&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer55987543" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12535300941422487594">Hmm. Well, I quite liked the beginning of this book and I felt like it had a lot of potential but I was a little disappointed that it developed into a story about a grudge between a woman and her evil mother-in-law. Really? Can't we get past that trope? Because, you know, women do nothing but fight with each other. And over what? A man, of course, namely Daniel, the son/husband. Because women don't do anything that doesn't have to do with men. Because women are irrational, see. HYSTerical. Ho ho</span>
  <span id="freeText12535300941422487594" style="display:none">Hmm. Well, I quite liked the beginning of this book and I felt like it had a lot of potential but I was a little disappointed that it developed into a story about a grudge between a woman and her evil mother-in-law. Really? Can't we get past that trope? Because, you know, women do nothing but fight with each other. And over what? A man, of course, namely Daniel, the son/husband. Because women don't do anything that doesn't have to do with men. Because women are irrational, see. HYSTerical. Ho ho ho.<br /><br />Also I was so annoyed that Meridia went back to Daniel at the end of the book. I'm completely drawing an uninformed overarching statement here, but I feel like unconvincing romantic plotlines are par for course in all the magical realism I've read (which really is just this book and The Alchemist). Okay, they're supposed to be madly in love because he sang to her, or whatever, but he's a complete wimp who never seems able to learn that his mother is atrocious. Daniel could have done with some deeper character development. Like, some internal angst over loving his mother but realizing she's an evil crazy woman, would have been good. Instead we come to the simplistic conclusion that Daniel is just a rube.<br /><br />And actually, what *about* Eva? It's kind of implied that she's actually really lonely and insecure but how cool would this book have been if the whole thing had had themes of woman's inhumanity to woman and the similarities between Eva, Meridia, and Rowenna and how the choices society presented them with created them?<br /><br />Also, what is the deal with Hannah floating in and out and implying that she and Meridia are in love and then disappearing for hundreds of pages before showing up again, just as inexplicably? I almost want to say that Meridia ought to have kicked Daniel to the curb and had herself a nice affair with Hannah, except that all the disappearing and running away and inexplicability implies that Hannah would have been completely closeted and thus just as infuriating as Thickhead Daniel. By the time she showed up at the end and then was summarily dropped (or disappeared again) I was fairly annoyed with her too. Also, why is Hannah invisible to everyone else? Are we supposed to conclude that Meridia has dreamed her up as an unreliable, flaky, and confusingly flirty friend as a remedy to her isolation and depression?<br /><br />Whatever. I know I totally just reamed the book but it was good mostly. It was well written, it's just that, for a book about women, it didn't do a whole of new stuff with the topic. The imagery and all that magical realism stuff was well done, atmospheric and all that. And kudos I guess for including Hannah at all, as well as not being shy about portraying Meridia as someone who desires, not just as an object of desire. And I'm predisposed to like generational stories of women's families after all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12535300941422487594" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10792568000689100977">So this is what I've learned about women in reading this book: they're spiteful, abusive, cold and with-holding from their husbands, are the cause of adultery, must be ice queens, servants, or whores, can't have a baby ever...seriously, every birth scene in this book resulted in death, blood, or curses, and every woman was an extreme; absolutely rage-filled or flat and meek and submissive. <br/>Women, in this book, are worried about by others if, after their baby dies, they are no longer interested i</span>
  <span id="freeText10792568000689100977" style="display:none">So this is what I've learned about women in reading this book: they're spiteful, abusive, cold and with-holding from their husbands, are the cause of adultery, must be ice queens, servants, or whores, can't have a baby ever...seriously, every birth scene in this book resulted in death, blood, or curses, and every woman was an extreme; absolutely rage-filled or flat and meek and submissive. <br />Women, in this book, are worried about by others if, after their baby dies, they are no longer interested in fashion and furniture. <br />If you are an independent woman, most likely you're at war with another woman. Or deceiving another one. Maybe setting bees on her while she's, you guessed it, trying to have a baby. And failing at it. The fact that this magical town even has people in it surprises me with all the lack of babies or mothers to raise them. <br />Also, what I learned, if your father embarrasses you in front of his friends, just start your period. Yep. Just gush all over your skirt. <br />Holy hell. <br />This author needs to put some serious time into how to write female characters. Even in a magical realist setting, we aren't that flat, insipid, revolting, dumb, and jealous. As beautiful as his words were in areas, I was offended by how horribly he got it wrong when he had at least NINE female characters and not one worthy of being on paper.</span>

  <span id="freeText12915319797120771473" style="display:none">I can tell from the overall review scoring on this book (as if I wouldn’t know from the book itself) that this will be a book most will be divided into two categories- loved it and found it to be drivel. Put me firmly into the loved it category, please. <br /><br />This book is hard to categorize - one part magical realism, one part fable, one part legend. It’s hard to tell the time or place that it takes place but if you are someone who loved the book you can describe the town, its streets, it’s familiar places. This is a fragrant story about the power of women, love, hate, and resentment. This is a rich heaping of the criticism we heap upon our parents and how crippling it’s effect can be. An eyeful of how our words can sting and sicken others. The characters are beautifully detailed in their personalities. <br /><br />I do not do spoilers but I will tell you the title of the book is very tied in with the book. <br /><br />This is a debut novel and I hope that this young man (who MUST have come from a multicultural background which would explain the variety of backgrounds he would have had to draw upon to write such an amazing book) has more like this in him.<br /><br />Big fan of this book and think a second read through would reveal more. <br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1580787446" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer5520108628177641260">This book is a solid 4+, but not a 5. I liked many aspects of it, but Eva was too much for me. Perhaps if there was some mitigating reason for her behavior, but as it was she tried to destroy the lives of everyone around her, stinging them with her vitriol, and that took a lot of enjoyment away for me. She seemed to embody every negative behavior, but did not feel like like an authentic character when put along side the others who were fully human & were mixes of good and bad. Magical realism fo</span>
  <span id="freeText5520108628177641260" style="display:none">This book is a solid 4+, but not a 5. I liked many aspects of it, but Eva was too much for me. Perhaps if there was some mitigating reason for her behavior, but as it was she tried to destroy the lives of everyone around her, stinging them with her vitriol, and that took a lot of enjoyment away for me. She seemed to embody every negative behavior, but did not feel like like an authentic character when put along side the others who were fully human &amp; were mixes of good and bad. Magical realism for me is when an everyday world much like ours...this one felt like an old-fashioned Latin American city although that is never specified, but it felt like Allende and Marquez territory...where the magic exists as an organic part of everyone's lives...the magic is layered on top of what could exist anywhere. Fantasy is other-worldly, it exists outside of everyday life. <br />An excellent first novel, well-developed and fascinating. It kept me interested. </span>

<div id="review_55165978" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/55165978" />
    <a title="Quiltgranny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1873199-quiltgranny"><img alt="Quiltgranny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1263754747p2/1873199.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/55165978?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Quiltgranny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Quiltgranny" href="/user/show/1873199-quiltgranny">Quiltgranny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1873199-quiltgranny?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer55165978" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10998655257221833120">What a surprise I received when I started reading this book. I actually was prepared to dislike it because I had read elsewhere that it is a fantasy, and I don't do well with that type of narrative.<br/><br/>BUT - as I continued to read on, the magical became real and accepted not only by the people in the story, but the reader as well. I was not bothered by the mist or the bees, or the fireflies or the "ghosts". Instead I saw them as allegorical for desire/emptiness, hatred, and personal reflections. The</span>
  <span id="freeText10998655257221833120" style="display:none">What a surprise I received when I started reading this book. I actually was prepared to dislike it because I had read elsewhere that it is a fantasy, and I don't do well with that type of narrative.<br /><br />BUT - as I continued to read on, the magical became real and accepted not only by the people in the story, but the reader as well. I was not bothered by the mist or the bees, or the fireflies or the "ghosts". Instead I saw them as allegorical for desire/emptiness, hatred, and personal reflections. The "ghosts" reminded me of Allende's House of Spirits, though not quite as well executed.<br /><br />I was bothered a bit by not knowing where this story of two families took place - perhaps I missed it in the early pages. I had to go back several times to read the first 20 or so pages to get some people and events straightened out in my mind as well. Understanding the cultural intricacies might have helped it flow a bit better.<br /><br />All in all, a very nice book that I had a hard time leaving when it was time to sleep. And a very well done FIRST novel by a non-native English speaker. The author's story is a fascinating read as well!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10998655257221833120" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer229287090" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2925723895413877483">This is a great novel to study if you need an example of a painfully plodding storyline which conveys not one iota of emotion to the reader. Really. This is everything NOT to do as a writer. It is one of those novels that you want to give up on after page 5, saying--ugh, how did this thing get published?--but which you finish because you have promised your teenaged daughter (who read it) that you would. There are so few things you share with your teenaged daughter these days, and so you read ALL</span>
  <span id="freeText2925723895413877483" style="display:none">This is a great novel to study if you need an example of a painfully plodding storyline which conveys not one iota of emotion to the reader. Really. This is everything NOT to do as a writer. It is one of those novels that you want to give up on after page 5, saying--ugh, how did this thing get published?--but which you finish because you have promised your teenaged daughter (who read it) that you would. There are so few things you share with your teenaged daughter these days, and so you read ALL 404 lousy pages. <br /><br />Beware, unpublished literary novelists out there!! This is a novel to make you wonder if you live in a pit-of-a-world in which literature has once-and-for-all died and bad novels continue to be published and read at the sacrifice of your own earnest, and in many cases, GOOD, work! I myself am trying not to be blue, and rather to learn from Mr. Setiawan everything I hope never to do in a novel. <br /><br />Ugh. Ugh. (double ugh)</span>

<div id="review_1666363503" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1666363503" />
    <a title="Irene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1887310-irene"><img alt="Irene" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1666363503?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Irene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Irene" href="/user/show/1887310-irene">Irene</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1666363503" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2978917067873238956">With its magical elements, non-specific time frame and archetypical characters, this had the feel of a modern fairytale. Like most traditional fairytales, this story told of negative relationships overcome and the victim triumphing. I do not favor this genre of storytelling. It deliberately avoids much of the complexity, subtlety of literary elements and smart dialogue I enjoy. But, I suspect that those who do like this type of book will have a positive reaction to this novel. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_132350543" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/132350543" />
    <a title="Lyn Battersby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4582793-lyn-battersby"><img alt="Lyn Battersby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1290721363p2/4582793.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/132350543?book_show_action=true">Nov 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn Battersby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn Battersby" href="/user/show/4582793-lyn-battersby">Lyn Battersby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4582793-lyn-battersby?shelf=do-not-loan-out-even-to-friends">do-not-loan-out-even-to-friends</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer132350543" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18209529355014474362">I read a lot of Speculative Fiction, so felt a desperate need to dip into something a bit different. The label in the library classified Of Bees and Mist as a family saga, which sounded like the perfect palate cleanser.<br/><br/>To my surprise, Of Bees and Mist turned out not to just be a family saga, but also a fantasy saga. I found myself thoroughly engrossed within a few paragraphs and despite the arrival of a new grandchild in the household, managed to finish it within three days (a record in my house</span>
  <span id="freeText18209529355014474362" style="display:none">I read a lot of Speculative Fiction, so felt a desperate need to dip into something a bit different. The label in the library classified Of Bees and Mist as a family saga, which sounded like the perfect palate cleanser.<br /><br />To my surprise, Of Bees and Mist turned out not to just be a family saga, but also a fantasy saga. I found myself thoroughly engrossed within a few paragraphs and despite the arrival of a new grandchild in the household, managed to finish it within three days (a record in my house where I'm the busy mother of 5). <br /><br />This is the story of the harm families routinely do to one another. On the surface Meridea belongs to the average dysfunctional family. Her mother neglects her, her father emotionally abuses her. Her mother suffers from OCD while her father spends his time in the arms of a lover. The two only meet up once a day, for breakfast. They do not exchange a word. <br /><br />Meridea grows up amonst this dysfunction and yet somehow manages to emerge in one piece. She meets and marries Daniel, the son of a business man and his overbearing wife. Now Meridea's problems really start.<br /><br />Yes, yes, a commonplace saga, but what really sets this work apart is the tight interweaving of the spirit realm. The magic realism is so tight, so flawless, that it just seems to make sense. Setiawan's story-telling ability accomplished that which all Spec Fic authors crave, the ability to make the reader leave their disbelief at the door. I believed in the mists that carried Gabriel to his lover, then brought him home again. I believed in the bees that buzzed and stung and caused such awful migraines. I believed in the never ending staircase and the marigolds and lemon verbena.<br /><br />This is one of those rare cross-genre novels where if you were to remove one part of it, the other part would fall done. The family is the skeleton of this novel, the saga the flesh and the magic the soul that breathes life to the story as a whole.<br /><br />This year I read The Great Gatsby and considered it my discovery novel of the year. I'm afraid, however, that Of Bees and Mist has taken its place.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18209529355014474362" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_150364211" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/150364211" />
    <a title="Maria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/654797-maria"><img alt="Maria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1196635070p2/654797.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/150364211?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria" href="/user/show/654797-maria">Maria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer150364211" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14923885072470695601">I think my favorite part of this book is the cover, so lovely. Lots of little images hidden in the vines. The story is full of magical realism which is a style I adore. i think it was at its strongest when describing the talents of the people at the market. I really wanted to love the book, but I felt it got weaker as it went on. The dialogue was particularly unconvincing. And while I was excited by the number of female characters in the novel, I was dismayed that the so infrequently felt real. </span>
  <span id="freeText14923885072470695601" style="display:none">I think my favorite part of this book is the cover, so lovely. Lots of little images hidden in the vines. The story is full of magical realism which is a style I adore. i think it was at its strongest when describing the talents of the people at the market. I really wanted to love the book, but I felt it got weaker as it went on. The dialogue was particularly unconvincing. And while I was excited by the number of female characters in the novel, I was dismayed that the so infrequently felt real. In the end, I don't know what the whole journey was about. It was interesting to look at the bio at the end to find that not only was the author male, but he wasIndonesian although the novel is set in a quasi-Hispanic world. I think it's absolutely reasonable to be guided by you imagination outside of your experience ad certainly, I don't read novels to get the plain facts of someone's life. But I wonder if maybe he wasn't taking on too may challenges by setting his first novel with a character outside of sexual, racial, temporal (?) personal experience. It felt vacuous at the end and maybe it was on account of the external images being right and the internal experience being absolutely absent.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14923885072470695601" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_133018151" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/133018151" />
    <a title="Finooola" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2112772-finooola"><img alt="Finooola" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1536096048p2/2112772.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/133018151?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Finooola" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Finooola" href="/user/show/2112772-finooola">Finooola</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2112772-finooola?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer133018151" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9047752665297260581">I liked this book, but have to give it the the 3-star-treatment thanks to a feeling of ambiguity and loose ends I got from it. Don't get me wrong, I enjoyed certain ambiguous aspects of it, for example the way it was impossible to fix it in an analogous period in history. What I didn't like was the feeling that the characters were symbolic, and that I didn't grasp of what. In that sense, maybe the book was a bit too smart for me, and if that's the case then I am at fault *hangs head*. However, a</span>
  <span id="freeText9047752665297260581" style="display:none">I liked this book, but have to give it the the 3-star-treatment thanks to a feeling of ambiguity and loose ends I got from it. Don't get me wrong, I enjoyed certain ambiguous aspects of it, for example the way it was impossible to fix it in an analogous period in history. What I didn't like was the feeling that the characters were symbolic, and that I didn't grasp of what. In that sense, maybe the book was a bit too smart for me, and if that's the case then I am at fault *hangs head*. However, another thing that bugged me was even though the book was fantastical in so many (unexplained!) ways, the everyday goings on felt very much like a soap opera, or worse, real life. The outlandish things that happen in this book may not happen in everyday life, but anyone on earth, unless they have literally no family, would recognise and roll their eyes at a lot of the feuding in the story. There is nothing wrong with books about the wrangles of everyday families of course, it's just that I don't go out of my way to read them, and was not expecting this to be one. About the loose ends, for the first 200 or so pages I was waiting for the book to click into place, before realising it was never going to. Again, I am at odds with some of the reviews I read so maybe I just didn't get it. I'm going around in circles insulting then making excuses for the book, but I have to finish by saying this book sets out to be an adult fairy tale. Not adult in the xxx sense just to be clear. And as such the characters should be larger than life and somewhat inexplicable, as well the events. I got that, and appreciated it, it just didn't work on the whole for me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9047752665297260581" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_61530567" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/61530567" />
    <a title="Elaine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2387638-elaine"><img alt="Elaine" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/61530567?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elaine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elaine" href="/user/show/2387638-elaine">Elaine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer61530567" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12470937953012303130">It is hard to believe that this is Erick Setiawan's first book. It is well written with reality, symbolism, mysticism and fantasy. This is not my usual choice of reading material but I found I was drawn into the book by the end of the first chapter. I found it difficult to put down, wanting to figure out the mysterious aspects, and to see what happens to the characters with pity, admiration and hopes of redemption. The writing style is one that I love in a book, because it does not spell out eve</span>
  <span id="freeText12470937953012303130" style="display:none">It is hard to believe that this is Erick Setiawan's first book. It is well written with reality, symbolism, mysticism and fantasy. This is not my usual choice of reading material but I found I was drawn into the book by the end of the first chapter. I found it difficult to put down, wanting to figure out the mysterious aspects, and to see what happens to the characters with pity, admiration and hopes of redemption. The writing style is one that I love in a book, because it does not spell out every detail for you, therefore being able to imagine the place and time in your own way. It is a made up world that could be in any country and in almost any time. I was so entranced with the book that I had read it in 1 1/2 weeks instead of the scheduled 4 weeks, and then read it again. I am glad to have had the chance to read this and I will most likely reread the book to catch things that I did not the first 2 times. I was unable to read for the past 5 years and feel very privlaged to have been able to read this book for my return. I have already and will continue to suggest this book as a wonderful read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12470937953012303130" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
